assuming continued compliance with various requirements of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended:  (i) interest 
on the 2021 Series B Bonds will not be included in the gross income of holders of such 2021 Series B Bonds for federal 
income tax purposes; and (ii) interest on the 2021 Series B Bonds is not a specific preference item for purposes of computation 
of the alternative minimum tax imposed on certain individuals.  Interest on the 2021 Series A Bonds will be included in the 
gross income of holders of such 2021 Series A Bonds for federal income tax purposes.  In the opinion of Bond Counsel, under 
existing law, interest on the 2021 Bonds and any profit made on the sale thereof are exempt  from Massachusetts personal 
income taxes, and the 2021 Bonds are exempt from Massachusetts personal property taxes.  See “TAX MATTERS” herein.

 The 2021 Series A Bonds (the “2021 Series A Bonds”) and Series B Bonds (the “2021 Series B Bonds” and, 
collectively with the 2021 Series A Bonds, the “2021 Bonds”) w ill bear interest from their date of delivery at the rates per

November 1 and will mature on November 1 in the years and in  the principal amounts set forth on the inside front cover. 
Purchases of the 2021 Bonds will be made in book-entry form only, in denominations of $5,000 or any integral multiple 
thereof.   
 The 2021 Bonds will be issued as fully registered bonds by means of a book-entry only system evidencing ownership 
and transfer thereof on the reco rds of The Depository Trust Company (“DTC”) an d its participants.  Principal of and semi-
annual interest on the 2021 Bonds are payable as described herein. 
 The dated dates, maturity dates, principal amounts, interest rates and prices or yields for the 2021 Bonds are set forth 
on the inside cover page of this Official Statement.  The 2021 Series B Bonds are subject to redemption prior to maturity, as 
described herein.  See THE 2021 SERIES B BONDS - “Redemption Provisions” herein. 
 The 2021 Bonds will constitute general obligations  of the Boston Water and Sewer Commission (the 
“Commission” or “BWSC”), issued and secured under the Commission’s General Bond Resolution (as defined 
herein).  The Commission has no taxing  power.  Neither the City of Boston  (the “City”) nor The Commonwealth of 
Massachusetts (the “Commonwealth”) no r any other political subdivision th ereof other than the Commission is 
obligated to pay the principal of and interest on the 2021 Bonds and neither the faith and credit nor the taxing power 
of the City or the Commonwealth or any such other politic al subdivision thereof is pled ged to such payment.  The 
Commission has the power to set rates and charges indepe ndently.  Such rates and charges are not subject to the 
regulation or approval of any department, board, or agency of the Commonwealth or of the City.

LLP, Boston, Massachusetts.  UniBank Fiscal Advisory Serv ices, Inc., Boston, Massachusetts, has acted as Municipal 
Advisor to the Commission with respect to the 2021 Bonds.  Settlement of the 2021 Bonds is expected on or about July 7, 
2021, at The Depository Trust Company in New York, New York or its custodial agent.

This Official Statement, which incl udes the cover page, the inside cover page and the appendices hereto, 
provides certain information in connection with th e issue by the Boston Water and Sewer Commission (the 
“Commission” or “BWSC”) of its $157,710,000 General Revenue and Refunding Bonds (Senior Series) 2021 Series A 
(Green Bonds) (Federally Taxable) (the “2021 Series A Bonds”) and $40,630,000 General Revenue and Refunding 
Bonds (Senior Series) 2021 Series B (the “2021 Series B Bonds”). The 2021 Series A Bonds and the 2021 Series B 
Bonds (collectively, the “2021 Bonds”) are to be issued under and secured by the Commission’s General Revenue Bond 
Resolution adopted on December 6, 1984, as amended a nd supplemented (the “General Bond Resolution”) and, 
respectively, the Twenty-Eighth and Twenty-Ninth Supplemental Resolutions (together, the “Supplemental 
Resolutions”), adopted by the Commission on March 24, 2021. The General Bond Resolution as amended and as 
supplemented by the Supplemental Resolutions is referred to  herein collectively as the “Resolution.”  The Resolution 
constitutes a contract between the Commission and U.S. Bank National Association, Boston, Massachusetts, as trustee 
(together with its successors, th e “Trustee”) on behalf of the owners of all bonds issued, or to be issued, under the 
General Bond Resolution, including the 2021 Bonds (collectively, the “Bonds”).  A glossary of certain terms used in 
this Official Statement and the Resolution is set forth in APPENDIX E.  The capitalization of any word herein not 
conventionally capitalized indicates that such word is defined in the Resolution or this Official Statement.  
The 2021 Series A Bonds are being issued (i) to advance refund certain maturities of the Commission’s 
outstanding Bonds (collectively, the “Advance Refunded Bonds”) and (ii) to provide for the payment of costs of issuance 
of the 2021 Series A Bonds.  The Advance Refunded Bonds include portions of the Commission’s General Revenue 
and Refunding Bonds (Senior Series), 2012 Series A, maturing in the years 2024 through 2034, inclusive,
 and 2037, its 
General Revenue Bonds (Senior Series), 2014 Series A, maturing in the years 2028, 2030 through 2035, inclusive, and 
2037, its General Revenue and Refunding Bonds (Senior Series), 2016 Series B, maturing in the years 2025 through 
2036, inclusive, and its General Revenue Bonds (Senior Seri es), 2018 Series A, maturing in the years 2035 through 
2037, inclusive.  See PLAN OF FINANCING.  
The 2021 Series B Bonds are being issued (i) to permanently finance certain capital improvements previously 
financed by outstanding commercial paper issued by the Commission and (ii) to provide for the payment of costs of 
issuance of the 2021 Series B Bonds.  See PLAN OF FINANCING.  
The 2021 Series A Bonds will be designated as “Green Bonds” and are the first such issue by the Commission.  
See “DESIGNATION AS GREEN BONDS” herein.

COVID-19 STATEMENT 
The outbreak of COVID-19, a respiratory disease caused by a new strain of coronavirus, was declared a pandemic by the 
World Health Organization in early 2020.  The President of the United States, and state and local governments in the United 
States, including the Commonwealth and the City of Boston, issued declarations of emergency to enable and empower 
governments in coordinating response to the spread of COVID-19.  Federal, state and local governments, including the 
Commonwealth and the City, as well as other nations and private businesses, issued restrictions on non-essential movement, 
gatherings, travel and other activities.  On March 10, 2020, Governor Charles Baker declared a state of emergency in the 
Commonwealth to provide more flexibility to respond to th e evolving outbreak of COVID-19 in Massachusetts.  On 
March 15, 2020, Mayor Martin J. Walsh announced that the City’s Public Health Commission declared a public health 
emergency in the City. Following on this announcement, the City of Boston has taken a number of steps to protect public 
health and safety. The continued spread of COVID-19 may adversely impact the economy of the Commonwealth and 
the City, as well as the nation. The Commission cannot predict at this time the extent or duration of any such impact. 
The Commission continues to monitor the situation and will coordinate as and when appropriate with Commonwealth, 
City and other public health officials and with community health care resources. 
 
As of May 29, 2021, all COVID-19 restrictions have been lifted throughout the City and the Commonwealth.  
 
The Commission is considered an “essential business” and as such, daily functions have been, and continue to be 
conducted.  Access to the Commission’s facilities by the pub lic are limited to Tuesdays and Fridays by appointment 
only.  The Commission’s billing and collections efforts are substantially continuing as normal.  Customers have the 
ability to pay online or by mail.  The Commission has temporarily suspended residential water service terminations.  Up 
until the end of calendar 2020, the Commission refrained from adding delinquency charges to any late bills.  The 
Commission reinstated delinquency charges effective January 1, 2021. 
 
Water consumption and wastewater flows decreased during 2020 as a result of the pandemic.  Among its twenty largest 
customers, five are major hospitals (Partners (Massachusetts General), Boston Medical Center, Brigham and Women’s 
Hospital, Beth Israel Hospital, and Ch ildren’s Hospital). The Commission has seen normal to increased usage from 
these institutions, which have been fully engaged in managing th e crisis over the past year. Four of the twenty largest 
customers are institutions of higher education (Boston Univ ersity, Northeastern University, Harvard University, and 
Boston College). These institutions reduced on-site operations and as a result, usage was reduced during most of calendar 
year 2020 and the beginning of calendar year 2021. Most of these institutions expect to return to full on-campus activity 
in the fall of 2021. The Commission’s fourth largest user  is the Massachusetts Port Authority, which operates Logan 
International Airport and Boston’s seaport facilities. Decreased aviation activity due to the crisis at the beginning of the 
pandemic led to decreased usage activity at the Port Au thority, however over the last several months activity has 
increased at the Port Authority to almost near pre-pandemic levels. 
 
For Fiscal Year 2020 (unaudited), the Commission’s revenues were less than projected which was largely attributable 
to lower usage caused by the COVID-19 pandemic. In re sponse, the Commission utilized certain Reserved Revenues 
available under the Resolution to support its operations. The Commission believes it has sufficient resources to support 
any short term financial and operational impact.  The extent to which the coronavirus impacts the financial and 
operations of the Commission will depend on future devel opments. The U.S. Congress passed the Coronavirus Aid, 
Relief, and Economic Security Act (the “CARES Act”) which was signed into law on March 27, 2020 and the American 
Rescue Plan (the “ARP”) Act of 2021, which was signed into law on March 11, 2021. Additional federal and state 
legislation responsive to the COVID-19 pandemic is currently under consideration and such legislation may include 
new forms of relief and additional resources responsive to COVID-19 to be made available to utilities and other public 
governmental entities. The Projected Revenues, Expenses and Coverage presented herein do not anticipate the receipt 
of any such federal or state funds.   
3 
INTRODUCTION 
The Commission was established in 1977 pursuant to a “home rule” petition adopted by the City of Boston (the 
“City”) and enacted by the Legislature of The Commonwealth of Massachusetts (the “Commonwealth”) as the Boston 
Water and Sewer Reorganization Act of 1977, Chapter 436 of the Acts of 1977 of the Commonwealth (the “Act”).  
Under the Act, the Commission has been constituted as a public instrumentality, a body politic and corporate and a 
political subdivision of the Commonwealth.  The Act provided for the transfer to the Commission of the ownership and 
responsibility for the operation of the water distribution syst em (the “Water Distribution System”) and the wastewater 
collection and stormwater drainage systems (the “Sewer System”) of the City.  The Wa ter Distribution System, which 
includes approximately 1,007 miles of pipe, and the Sewer System, which includes approximately 1,536 miles of sewers, 
serve approximately 90,000 acco unts.  For the purpose of this document , “Systems” includes the Water Distribution 
System (including potable water and fire suppression facilitie s), the Sewer System (including separate sanitary sewer, 
separate stormwater drains and combined sewers), and the related appurtenances and fixtures.  In 1978, the Commission 
assumed such ownership and responsibility for the provision of water distribution, wastewater collection, and 
stormwater drainage services, on a retail basis, to residen tial, commercial, industrial, public, private and non-profit 
institutional and other properties throughout the City. 
Under the Act, the Commission has the power to set its rates and charges independently.  The Act requires that 
such rates and charges be set at a level and amount suffic ient to meet the Commission’s obligations under the Act 
including, but not limited to, operating expenses, debt service on bonds of the Commission, all required reserves and 
assessments for bulk water supply, water distribution, wastewater treatment and sewage collection services obtained by 
the Commission, as discussed below.  These rates and charges are not subject to the regulation or approval of any 
department, board or agency of the Commonwealth or the City. 
The Commission’s fiscal year (the “Fiscal Year”) co rresponds to the calendar year.  The Commission has 
covenanted under the Resolution to maintain fees and charges in each Fiscal Year at levels sufficient to provide Net 
Revenues (as hereinafter defined) on a cash basis at least equal to 125% of the debt service during such Fiscal Year with 
respect to all outstanding Bonds, including the 2021 Bonds.  The Resolution establishes separate reserve funds for debt 
service, operations and maintenance, insurance and renewal and replacement expenditures, which funds, together with 
all other funds established by the Resolution (except the Subordinated Debt Service Reserve Fund, the General Fund 
and the Rebate Fund), are pledged as security for the Senior Bonds, including the 2021 Bonds, and (except for the Senior 
Debt Service Fund, Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund, Senior Redemption Account, Rebate Fund and the General 
Fund) as security for any outstanding Subordinated Bonds. Currently, there are no outstanding Subordinated Bonds. The 
Resolution also establishes a Stabilization Fund, which, as disc ussed below, is intended to mitigate the rate impact of 
extraordinary cost increases or declines in revenues.  The Stabilization Fund also is pledged as security for the Bonds. 
The Commission has realized surpluses from its operations in each year since its inception.  In accordance with 
the Act, the Commission applies audited surpluses to reduce its rates in succeed ing years.  Audited surpluses were 
realized and applied to reduce future rates in the amount of approximately $500,000 to $700,000 from 2015 to 2019.  
For Fiscal Year 2020, which is unaudited at this time, a surplus of approximately $430,000 is projected and expected to 
be applied to reduce rates in 2021.  To achieve this  result, the Commission applied approximately $19 million of 
Reserved Revenues from the Stabilization Fund. Historical debt service coverage has exceeded the 125% coverage level 
calculated on a cash basis as required under the Resolution. The Commission’s debt service coverage for all Outstanding 
Bonds over Fiscal Years 2015-2019 averaged 147%.  The debt service coverage for all Outstanding Bonds for Fiscal 
Year 2020 is projected to be approximately 137%.   
The Commission has a diverse and stable customer base  that includes residential, commercial, industrial, 
public, private and non-profit institutional properties throughout the City.  See FINANCIAL OPERATIONS –
“Customer Base.” As of December 31, 2020, such  tax-exempt entities accounted for approximately 23.9% of the 
Commission’s sales on a consumption basis.  Commercial facilities, such as office buildings and hotels, accounted for 
approximately 21.4% of sales, while approximately 2.7% of sales were to industrial users.  Approximately 29.4% of the 
Commission’s sales were generated from single, two, and three family residential properties. Larger, multi-family rental 
and condominium properties accounted for approximately 22.6% of sales. 
The Commission has a track record of increasing its rates and charges in a reasonable manner. In Fiscal Year 
2017, water and sewer rates were increased by 2.40%; in Fis cal Year 2018 there was an incr ease of 4.75%; in Fiscal 
Year 2019 there was an increase of 2.85%; and in Fiscal Year 2020 there was an increase of 7.90%. In Fiscal Year 2021 
the increase is 8.90% due to the reduc tion in customer usage during the COVID-19 pandemic.  The Commission is  
4 
projecting additional increases in Fiscal Years 2022 through 2025.  See FINANCIAL OPERATIONS - “Projected 
Revenues and Expenses.”   
The Commission has been experiencing a gradual reducti on in the amount of water that is billed to its 
customers.  Billed water has decreased from 68.0 million gall ons per day (“mgd”) in Fiscal Year 1997 to 52.8 mgd in 
Fiscal Year 2019. In large part due to the COVID-19 pandemic, billed water decreased to 49.4 mgd in Fiscal Year 2020, 
representing a 6.3% decrease over Fiscal Year 2019.  The re duction in water sales is attributed to water conservation 
efforts and to the increased use of water efficient fixtur es in residences and businesses throughout the City. The 
Commission understands that many other cities are also experiencing similar long-term reductions.  The reduced water 
sales have in part necessitated the rate increases in the past  decade and projected rate in creases in future years. See 
COVID-19 and HISTORICAL REVENUES AND EXPENSES. 
The Commission employs an integrated collection program, including a shut-off program for delinquent 
accounts, an automated reminder program and a property lien program.  As the Commission’s most recent rolling 12-
month collection rates reflect, such efforts have proved successful, and the Commission has been collecting virtually all 
amounts charged to its customers. As a result of the COVID-19 pandemic, certain aspects of the Commission’s 
collections activities were suspended on March 10, 2020 but were resumed as of January 1, 2021 with the exception of 
shut-offs.  See FINANCIAL OPERATIONS - “Collections.”  
The Commission’s improvements to the Water Distribution System since 1977 include the replacing or relining 
of approximately 641  miles of water mains, resulting in lower maintena nce costs and improved water service.  As a 
result of the Commission’s renewal and replacement, leak detection and metering prog rams, annual unbilled water, 
which is the difference between water purchased from th e Massachusetts Water Resources Authority (the “MWRA”) 
and water sold to customers, has been reduced from 70 mgd in Fiscal Year 1977 to 9.1 mgd in Fiscal Year in 2020, an 
87% reduction.  See HISTORICAL REVENUES AND EXPENSES – “MWRA Assessments to the Commission.” 
Improvements to the Sewer System made by the Commission in the past three decades have significantly 
increased the Sewer System’s capacity and eliminated dry-weather overflows of untreated sewage into Boston Harbor 
from combined sewers.  Major accomplishments in the 1980s and 1990s included the construction of the Boston Main 
and East Side Interceptors, the elimination of twelve co mbined sewer overflow outlets (“CSO”) and the rehabilitation 
of the Saint James Avenue Interceptor in the Back Bay section of the City using state of the art trenchless technologies.  
These sewer separation projects, in addition to other Commission sewer separation projects in the City, have yielded a 
reduction of CSOs and inflow into the Sewer System, resulting in significant savings to the Commission. As of June 30, 
2016, the CSO removal plan was completed and the Commi ssion has received approximately $290.3 million from the 
MWRA in support funding. 
The Commission expects to continue to fund necessary capital improvements to the Systems and its other 
property from various sources, includ ing proceeds of Bonds and Bond Anticip ation Notes (as hereinafter defined), 
available revenue from rates and charges, grant proceeds and loans under the loan program of the Massachusetts Clean 
Water Trust (the “MCWT”), the MWRA Infiltration and Inflow Local Financial Assistance Program (the “I/I 
Grant/Loan Program”) and the MWRA Local Water System  Assistance Program (the “LWSAP”).  Such capital 
improvements are included in the Commission’s Capital Im provement Program (the “CIP”) adopted annually by the 
Commission as provided by the Resolution.  Currently, the Commission has developed a CIP for 2021 through 2023 
encompassing $201.1 million of improvements, including expe nditures of approximately $72.0 million in Fiscal Year 
2021. See CAPITAL IMPROVEMENT PROGRAMS OF THE COMMISSION.  The Commission believes that its 
CIP will be sufficient to maintain its Systems in sound operating condition and meet current and projected demand for 
services. 
The Commission obtains its water supply and its wastewater treatment from the MWRA, a public 
instrumentality of the Commonwealth.  The MWRA currently is authorized to provide water supply services to 54 cities, 
towns, and special purpose entities, including the Commission, and wastewater treatment to nearly half the State’s 
population in 43 cities, towns, and special purpose entities,  including the Commission, located mostly in eastern 
Massachusetts (collectively, “Local Bodies”), all of which are assessed annual charges for such services.  
MWRA charges are payable in ten equal installments due on or before the first business day of each month 
excluding January and July.  The Commission is the MWRA’s single largest customer and MWRA assessments are the 
single largest component of the Commission’s operating expenses. The MWRA’s fiscal year (the “MWRA Fiscal Year”) 
ends June 30. For the MWRA Fiscal Year 2021, the Commission is projected to account for approximately 36.6% of 
the MWRA’s aggregate water assessmen ts and approximately 29.1% of the MWRA’s sewer assessments.  On a 
combined basis, the Commission’s projected MWRA water and sewer assessments represent approximately 31.7% of  
5 
MWRA Fiscal Year 2021 assessments.  See FINANCIAL OPERATIONS - “MWRA Assessments to the 
Commission.” 
The Commission and the MWRA, as well as other governmental bodies, have undertaken significant capital 
expenditure programs designed to address pollution in the Boston Harbor area. The MWRA’s total capital expenditures 
from its commencement of operations in 1985 through December 31, 2020 total more than $8.8 billion, which includes 
expenditures for both water and wastewater improvements.  The MWRA annually prepar es and updates its capital 
improvement program (the “MWRA CIP”). In June 2020, the MWRA’ Board of Directors (the “MWRA Board”) 
approved the MWRA CIP for the MWRA’s fiscal year 2021 (July 1, 2020 through June 30, 2021 (the “MWRA FY21 
CIP”), which includes spending for fiscal years 2019 through 2023, and projections beyond fiscal year 2023. The 
MWRA FY21 CIP includes a five-year capital baseline spending cap for MWRA fiscal years 2019 through 2023 of 
approximately $984.8 million, with projected spending of $905.1 million based on the MWRA FY21 CIP.  The MWRA 
expects that the MWRA Board will consider for approval an update to the MWRA CIP for fiscal year 2022 in or about 
June 2021. Projected MWRA capital expenditures not otherwise funded through federal grants or loans from the MCWT 
are expected to be funded by the MWRA through the issuance of bonds and other forms of indebtedness. The payment 
of the cost of such MWRA programs, including debt service for debt-financed MWRA capital expenditures, will be 
included in the MWRA’s assessments to its Local Bodies for the supply of water and sewer services. The Commission’s 
financial projections set forth herein reflect, among other things, current estimates of the costs of the MWRA’s programs, 
the availability of state and federal grants and loan funds, and assumptions concerning borrowing costs, based upon 
available public data and interviews with the staff and consultants to the MWRA and the Commission. A number of 
factors, including reductions or incr eases in the MWRA’s planned capital im provement program and reductions or 
increases in the availability of state and federal aid or in the Commission’s allocable share of the costs of such program, 
could cause substantial variations from the projected MWRA assessments to the Commission. See FINANCIAL 
OPERATIONS - “MWRA Assessments to the Commission”  and MASSACHUSETTS WATER RESOURCES 
AUTHORITY - “MWRA Capital Improvement Program.” 
MWRA assessments are budgeted by the Commission as operating expenses.  However, under the flow of 
funds established by the Resolution, payment of such MWRA assessments is subordinate to the payment of debt service 
on Senior Bonds and Subordinated Bonds, to the payment of other operating expenses and to the maintenance at required 
levels of reserve funds for debt service and other purposes.  See SECURITY FOR THE BONDS - “Flow of Funds.”  
MWRA assessments, on a rate basis, are projected to be approximately 62.9% and 61.6% of the Commission’s total 
operating expenses in Fiscal Year 2020 and Fiscal Year 2021, respectively.  According to MWRA projections, the 
Commission’s charges for MWRA Fiscal Years 2022 to 2025 will increase at an average annual rate of 3.5%.  Based 
on such MWRA projections, the Commission project s that MWRA assessments to the Commission will be 
approximately 62.2% of the Commission’s oper ating expenses for Fiscal Year 2025.  See FINANCIAL 
OPERATIONS – “MWRA Assessments to the Commission.” 
The Commission reviews its rates and charges annually in response to operating factors, including changes in 
MWRA assessments.  During Fiscal Years 2017 through 2021 , the Commission raised its water and sewer rates by an 
average annual rate of 5.4%.  The average combined rate per thousand gallons of water and wastewater, currently set at 
$22.54, is projected to increase to approximately $26.39 in  Fiscal Year 2025, representi ng an average annual rate of 
increase of 4.0%.  References in this Official Statement to the Commission’s rates are to the Commission’s combined 
water and sewer rates. 
Actual increases in both MWRA assessments to the Commission and the Commission’s rates and charges to 
its customers have varied in the past from prior projections , and future increases are likely also to vary from current 
projections.  Due to a variety of factors, including lower th an assumed rates of interest and inflation, changes in the 
timing of its capital improvem ent program, and the receipt of federal and state assistance, the MWRA’s aggregate 
assessments to the Local Bodies generally have been lower than original projections.  There is no assurance, however, 
that MWRA assessments will continue to be lower than original projections or that the Commission will be able to set 
rates at a level lower than anticipated in its current projections. 
The Commission maintains the option to use the Stabilization Fund established under the Resolution to mitigate 
the impact of annual increases  to its ratepayers.  The unaudited balance in the Stabilization Fu nd as of December 31, 
2020 was $42.6 million, which is substantially in excess of the currently existing Stabilization Fund requirement under 
the Resolution.  See SECURITY FOR THE BONDS - “Reserve Funds and Stabilization Fund.”  The Commission’s 
current projections call for deposits to the Stabiliza tion Fund in Fiscal Years 2022 through 2025.  See 
FINANCIAL 
OPERATIONS – “Stabilization Fund” and “MWRA Assessments to the Commission.”

The 2021 Series A Bonds and the 2021 Series B Bonds are the twenty-eighth and twenty-ninth series, 
respectively, of Bonds issued under the General Bond Re solution and will be secured by and entitled to the protection 
of the Resolution as Senior Bonds on a parity with all Outstanding Senior Bonds.  Upon issuance of the 2021 Bonds, 
the Commission expects to have Outstanding under the Resolution approximately $548 million of Senior Bonds and no 
Subordinated Bonds.  See FINANCIAL OPERATIONS - “Outstanding Indebtedness”  for a description of such 
Outstanding Bonds.  As more fully described herein, Additional Bonds are expected to be issued under the Resolution 
which, together with the 2021 Bonds and other Outstanding Bonds, will be secured by and entitled to the protection of 
the General Bond Resolution.  Such Additional Bonds may be issued under the General Bond Resolution either as Senior 
Bonds on a parity with the 2021 Bonds and other Outstanding Senior Bonds or as Subordinated Bonds on a parity with 
other Outstanding Subordinated Bonds, if any, and may be issued with or without credit enhancement.  The Bonds are 
general obligations of the Commission secured by a pledge of Revenues (as hereinafter defined) and other amounts 
under the Resolution.  From time to time the Commission issues Bond Anticipation Notes under a commercial paper 
program in order to temporarily finance capital improvements.  Such Bond Anticipation Notes are issued in anticipation 
of the issuance of Bonds, including the 2021 Series B Bonds, and are secured as to interest on a subordinated basis under 
the General Bond Resolution. A portion of the 2021 Series B Bonds will be applied to repay certain commercial paper 
Bond Anticipation Notes. Following such application, the Commission expects that no Bond Anticipation Notes will 
remain outstanding.  See SECURITY FOR THE BONDS. 
This Official Statement contains brief descriptions of the Commission, its operations, its finances, the Systems, 
the Commission’s CIPs, and other information, including a summary of the activities and the operations of the MWRA, 
the terms of the 2021 Bonds, the Resolution, and certain provisions of the Act, among other subjects.  For certain 
portions of this Official Statement the Commission has relied upon information provided by the MWRA.  See 
MASSACHUSETTS WATER RESOURCES AUTHORITY.  The summaries of and references to all documents, 
statutes, reports and other instruments referred to herein do not purport to be complete and each such document, statute, 
report or instrument is qualified in its entirety by reference to the original form thereof, copies of which are available 
from the Commission.  All references to the Bonds are qua lified in their entirety by reference to the definitive forms 
thereof and the information with respect thereto contained in the Resolution. 
PLAN OF FINANCING 
The net proceeds of the 2021 Series A Bonds and other funds available under the Resolution are expected to 
be applied (i) to advance refund the Advance Refunded Bonds and (ii) to pay costs of issuance of the 2021 Series A 
Bonds. Upon delivery of the 2021 Series A Bonds, a portion of the proceeds of the 2021 Series A Bonds will be deposited 
into the Refunding Escrow Fund established by an Escrow Agreement between the Commission and U.S. Bank National 
Association, as Escrow Agent. The Refunding Escrow Fund w ill be invested in United States government or agency 
obligations maturing in amounts and bearing interest at rates sufficient, without further reinvestment, to pay, when due, 
interest on, and upon redemption, the outstanding principal of and redemption premium, if any, on the Advance 
Refunded Bonds.  The Refunding Escrow Fund, including the in terest earnings on the obligations therein, is pledged 
solely for the benefit of the holders of the Advance Refunded Bonds and is not available to pay the principal of and 
interest on the 2021 Bonds. 
The net proceeds of the 2021 Series B Bonds and other funds available under the Resolution shall be applied 
(i) to retire outstanding commercial paper issued by the Commission and thereby permanently finance the capital 
improvements originally financed by such commercial paper and (ii) to pay costs of issuance of the 2021 Series B 
Bonds.

DESIGNATION AS GREEN BONDS 
The Commission has designated the 2021 Series A Bonds as “Green Bonds” due to the adherence of the projects 
refinanced by the 2021 Series A Bonds with the federal Safe Drinking Water Act and the Clean Water Act. The purpose 
of identifying the 2021 Series A Bonds as Green Bonds is to allow investors to invest directly in bonds that finance 
environmentally beneficial projects in the City.  The Green Bonds are issued on a parity with the 2021 Series B Bonds and 
other Senior Bonds issued by the Commission pursuant to the Resolution.  Holders of the Green Bonds do not assume any 
specific project risk related to any of the projects refunded with the proceeds of the Green Bonds. Descriptions of projects 
refunded with the proceeds of the Green Bonds are included in Appendix H – “Green Bond Project Descriptions.” 
The net proceeds of the Green Bonds are expected to be applied on the closing date to fund an escrow to defease 
the Advance Refunded Bonds.

a report on the mathematical accuracy of  certain computations, contained in schedules provided to them by the senior 
managing Underwriter, as confirmed by the Municipal Advisor, relating to the adequacy of the maturing principal 
amounts of the obligations held by the Escrow Agent and in terest to be earned thereon to pay all the principal, 
redemption premium, where applicable, and interest on the Advance Refunded Bonds when due.

Redemption Provisions 
Optional Redemption of the 2021 Series A Bonds at Par  
The 2021 Series A Bonds maturing after November 1, 2031 are subject to redemption at the option of the 
Commission, on or after November 1, 2031 as a whole or in part at any time, from maturities selected by the Commission 
at a redemption price equal to 100% of the principal amount to be redeemed, plus accrued interest to the date of 
redemption. 
Optional Redemption of the 2021 Series A Bonds with Make-Whole Payment 
The 2021 Series A Bonds maturing on or before November 1, 2031 are subject to redemption at the option of 
the Commission, as a whole or in part at any time, from maturities selected by the Commission at the Make-Whole 
Redemption Price. The “Make-Whole Redemption Price” is the greater of (i) 100% of the principal amount of the 2021 
Series A Bonds to be redeemed or (ii) the sum of the present value of the remaining scheduled payments of principal 
and interest on the 2021 Series A Bonds to be redeemed, not including any portion of those payments of interest accrued 
and unpaid as of the date fixed for the redemption (the “Scheduled Redemption Date”), discounted to the Scheduled 
Redemption Date on a semi-annual basis, assuming a 360-day year consisting of twelve 30-day months, at the Treasury 
Rate (as defined below) plus 15 basis points. 
For purpose of determining the Make-Whole Redemption Price, the following definitions apply: 
“Treasury Rate” means, with respect to any Scheduled Redemption Date for any particular 2021 Series A Bond, 
the greater of: 
(i) the yield to maturity as of the Schedule d Redemption Date of the United States Treasury 
securities with a constant maturity (as compiled and published in th e most recent Federal Reserve Statistical 
Release H.15 (519) that has become publicly available at least two (2) business days prior to the Scheduled 
Redemption Date (excluding inflation indexed securities) (or, if such Statistical Release is no longer published, 
any publicly available source of similar market data)) most nearly equal to the period from the Scheduled 
Redemption Date to maturity; provided, however, that if the period from the Scheduled Redemption Date to 
maturity is less than one year, th e weekly average yield on actually tr aded United States Treasury securities 
adjusted to a constant maturity of one year will be used; all as will be determined by an independent accounting 
firm, investment banking firm or financial advisor retained by the Commission at the Commission’s expense, 
which determination shall be conclusive and binding on the owners of the 2021 Series A Bonds; or 
(ii) the rate per annum, expressed as a percentage of the principal amount, equal to the 
semiannual equivalent yield to maturity or interpolated maturity of the Comparable Treasury Issue (as defined 
below), assuming that the Comparable Treasury Issue is purchased on the Scheduled Redemption Date for a 
price equal to the Comparable Treasury Price (as defi ned below), as calculated by the Designated Investment 
Banker (as defined below); 
plus, in either case, accrued and unpaid interest to the Scheduled Redemption Date. 
“Comparable Treasury Issue” means, with respect to any Scheduled Redemption Date for a particular 2021 
Series A Bond, the United States Treasury security or securities selected by the Designated Investment Banker that has 
an actual or interpolated maturity comparable to the remaining average life of the 2021 Series A Bond to be redeemed. 
“Comparable Treasury Price” means, with respect to any Scheduled Redemption Date for a particular 2021 
Series A Bond, (i) if the Designated Investment Banker receives at least four (4) Reference Treasury Dealer Quotations 
(as defined below), the average of such quotations for such Scheduled Redemption Date, after excluding the highest and 
lowest Reference Treasury Dealer Quotations, or (ii) if the Designated Investment Banker obtains fewer than four (4) 
Reference Treasury Dealer Quotations, the average of all such quotations. 
“Designated Investment Banker” means one of the Reference Treasury Dealers appointed by the Commission.  
9 
“Reference Treasury Dealer” means each of the four firm s, specified by the Commission from time to time, 
that are primary United States government securities dealer s in the City of New York, New York (each  a “Primary 
Treasury Dealer”); provided, however, that if any of them ceases to be a Primary Treasury Dealer, the Commission will 
substitute another Primary Treasury Dealer. 
“Reference Treasury Dealer Quotations ” means, with respect to each Re ference Treasury Dealer and any 
Scheduled Redemption Date for a particular 2021 Series A Bond, the average, as dete rmined by the Designated 
Investment Banker, of the bid and asked prices for the Comparable Treasury Issue (expressed in each case as a 
percentage of its principal amount) quoted in writing to the Designated Investment Banker by such Reference Treasury 
Dealer at 3:30 P.M., New York City time, on the third (3rd) business day preceding such Scheduled Redemption Date. 
Any Make-Whole Redemption Price of 2021 Series A Bonds to be redeemed pursuant to the provisions 
described under this section will be determined by an independent accounting firm, investment banking firm or financial 
advisor retained by the Commission to calculate such redemption price. The Commission may conclusively rely on the 
determination of such redemption price by such independen t accounting firm, investment banking firm or financial 
advisor and will not be liable for such reliance. 
Optional Redemption of the 2021 Series B Bonds at Par 
The 2021 Series B Bonds maturing after November 1, 2031 are subject to redemption at the option of the 
Commission, on or after November 1, 2031 as a whole or in part at any time, from maturities selected by the Commission 
at a redemption price equal to 100% of the principal amount to be redeemed, plus accrued interest to the date of 
redemption.

Selection of 2021 Bonds for Redemption 
2021 Series A Bonds.  So long as the 2021 Series A Bonds are held in the book-entry only system, if fewer than 
all the 2021 Series A Bonds of a particular maturity are to be redeemed, the particular 2 021 Series A Bonds of such 
maturity or portions thereof to be redeemed shall be allocated on a pro rata pass-through distribution of principal basis 
in accordance with DTC procedures, provided that so long as the 2021 Series A Bonds are held in book-entry form, the 
selection for redemption of such 2021 Series A Bonds of such maturity shall be made in accordance with the operational 
arrangements of DTC then in effect and, if the DTC operational arrangements do not allow for redemption on a pro rata 
pass-through distribution of principal basis, the 2021 Series A Bonds of such maturity will be selected for redemption, 
in accordance with DTC procedures, by lot. If the 2021 Series A Bonds are no longer held in the book-entry only system 
and fewer than all the 2021 Series A Bonds of a particular maturity are to be redeemed, the particular 2021 Series A 
Bonds or portions thereof to be for redeemed shall be allocated by the Paying Agent on a pro rata pass-through 
distribution of principal basis as provided in the Resolution.  
The Commission intends that redemption allocations made by DTC with respect to the 2021 Series A Bonds 
of a maturity be made on a pro rata pass-through distribution of principal basis as described above.  However, the 
Commission cannot provide any assurance that DTC, DTC’s direct and indirect participants or any other intermediary 
will allocate the redemption of 2021 Series A Bonds of such maturity on such basis.  
2021 Series B Bonds.  So long as the 2021 Series B Bonds are held in the book-entry only system, if fewer than 
all the 2021 Series B Bonds of a particul ar maturity are to be redeemed, the pa rticular 2021 Series B Bonds of such 
maturity (or portions thereof in authorized denominations) to be redeemed shall be sel ected in accordance with DTC 
procedures, by lot. If the 2021 Series B Bonds are no longer  held in the book-entry only system and fewer than all the 
2021 Series B Bonds of a particular maturity are to be redeemed, the particular 2021 Series B Bonds (or portions thereof 
in authorized denominations) to be redeemed shall be selected by the Paying Agent as provided in the Resolution. The 
Paying Agent shall select 2021 Series B Bonds by lot or in any customary manner as determined by the Paying Agent. 
Notice of Redemption 
Notice of redemption of the 2021 Bonds shall be mailed or conveyed electronically to the registered owners of 
any 2021 Bonds which are to be redeemed which, so long as  the book-entry only system is in effect, shall mean DTC 
or its nominee as described below under “Book-Entry Only System” at the address shown on the registration books 
kept by the Paying Agent, not less than 30 and not more than 45 days prior to the redemption date. Notice of redemption 
shall identify the 2021 Bonds to be redeemed, state the date fixed for redemption, and state that such 2021 Bonds will 
be redeemed at the office of the Paying Agent. The notice of redemption shall further state that on such date there shall 
become due and payable upon each 2021 Bond (or portion thereof) to be redeemed, the redemption price thereof, 
together with interest accrued to the re demption date. Moneys therefor having be en deposited with the Paying Agent, 
interest on any 2021 Bond called for redemption shall cease  to accrue from and after the date fixed for redemption. 
Failure to mail notice to a particular Bondowner, or any defect in the notice to such Bondowner, shall not affect the 
redemption of any other 2021 Bonds.
 
Book-Entry Only System 
The information in this section concerning Depository  Trust Company, New York, New York (“DTC”), and 
DTC’s book entry system has been obtained from sources that the Commission believes to be reliable, but neither the 
Commission nor the Underwriters takes any responsibility for the accuracy or completeness thereof. 
The Commission and the Underwriters cannot and do not give any assurances that DTC, Participants or others 
will properly distribute: (i) payments of debt service on th e 2021 Bonds paid to DTC, or its nominee owner, as the 
registered owners; or (ii) any redemption or other notices, to the Beneficial Owners, or that they will do so on a timely 
basis or that DTC will serve and act in the manner described in this Official Statement. 
DTC will act as securities depository for the 2021 Bonds.   The 2021 Bonds will be issued as fully-registered 
securities registered in the name of Cede & Co. (DTC’s partnership nominee) or such other name as may be requested 
by an authorized representative of DTC.   One fully-registered 2021 Bond certificate will be issued for each maturity 
(and interest rate, if applicable) of the 2021 Series A Bonds  and of the 2021 Series B Bonds in the aggregate principal 
amount of such maturity (and interest rate, if applicable),  of such 2021 Bonds as set forth on the inside cover page 
hereof, and will be deposited with DTC.  
11 
DTC, the world’s largest securities depository, is a limited-purpose trust company organized under the New 
York Banking Law, a “banking organization” within the meaning of the New York Banking Law, a member of the 
Federal Reserve System, a “clearing corporation” within the meaning of the New York Uniform Commercial Code, and 
a “clearing agency” registered pursuant to the provisions of Section 17A of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934.  DTC 
holds and provides asset servicing for over 3.5 million issues of U.S. and non-U.S. equity issues, corporate and municipal 
debt issues, and money market instruments (from over 100 countries) that DTC’s participants (“Direct Participants”) 
deposit with DTC.  DTC also facilitates the post-trade settlement among Direct Participants of sales and other securities 
transactions in deposited securities, through electronic computerized book-entry transfers and pledges between Direct 
Participants’ accounts.  This eliminates the need for physical  movement of securities certifi cates.  Direct Participants 
include both U.S. and non-U.S. securities brokers and dealers, banks, trust companies, clearing corporations, and certain 
other organizations.  DTC is a wholly-owned subsidiary of The Depository Trust & Clearing Corporation (“DTCC”).  
DTCC is the holding company for DTC, National Secur ities Clearing Corporation and Fixed Income Clearing 
Corporation, all of which are registered clearing agencies.  DTCC is owned by th e users of its regulated subsidiaries.  
Access to the DTC system is also available to others such as both U.S. and n on-U.S. securities br okers and dealers, 
banks, trust companies, and clearing corp orations that clear through or maintain  a custodial relationship with a Direct 
Participant, either directly or indirectly (“Indirect Par ticipants”).  DTC has an S&P Global Ratings (“S&P”) rating of 
AA+.  The DTC Rules applicable to its Participants are on file with the Securities and Exchange Commission.  More 
information about DTC can be found at www.dtcc.com.  
Purchases of 2021 Bonds under the DTC system must be made by or through Direct Participants, which will 
receive a credit for the 2021 Bonds on DTC’s records.  The ownership interest of each actual purchaser of each 2021 
Bond (“Beneficial Owner”) is in turn to be recorded on the Direct and Indirect Participants’ records.  Beneficial Owners 
will not receive written confirmation from DTC of their purchase.  Beneficial Owners are, however, expected to receive 
written confirmations providing details of the transaction, as well as periodic statements of their holdings, from the 
Direct or Indirect Participant through which the Beneficial Owner entered into the transaction.  Transfers of ownership 
interests in the 2021 Bonds are to be accomplished by entrie s made on the books of Direct and Indirect Participants 
acting on behalf of Beneficial Owners.  Beneficial Owners  will not receive certificates  representing their ownership 
interests in Bonds, except in the event that use of the book-entry system for the 2021 Bonds is discontinued. 
To facilitate subsequent transfers, all 2021 Bonds deposited by Direct Participants with DTC are registered in 
the name of DTC’s partnership nominee, Cede & Co. or such other name as may be requested by an authorized 
representative of DTC.  The deposit of 2021 Bonds with DTC and their registration in the name of Cede & Co. or such 
other DTC nominee do not affect any change in beneficial ownership.  DTC has no knowledge of the actual Beneficial 
Owners of the 2021 Bonds; DTC’s reco rds reflect only the identity of the Dir ect Participants to whose accounts such 
2021 Bonds are credited, which may or may not be the Benefi cial Owners.  The Direct and Indirect Participants will 
remain responsible for keeping account of their holdings on behalf of their customers. 
Conveyance of notices and other communications by DTC to Direct Participants, by Direct Participants to 
Indirect Participants, and by Direct Par ticipants and Indirect Participants to Beneficial Owners will be governed by 
arrangements among them, subject to any statutory or regulatory requirements as may be in effect from time to time. 
Redemption notices shall be sent to DTC.  If less than all of the 2021 Series A Bonds or 2021 Series B Bonds 
of like maturity and interest rate are being redeemed, DTC’s practice is to determine by lot the amount of the interest of 
each Direct Participant in such maturity and interest rate to be redeemed. 
Neither DTC nor Cede & Co. (nor any other DTC nominee) will consent or vote with respect to 2021 Bonds 
unless authorized by a Direct Participant in accordance with DTC’s MMI Procedures.  Under its usual procedures, DTC 
mails an Omnibus Proxy to the Trustee as soon as possible after the record date.  The Omnibus Proxy assigns Cede & 
Co.’s consenting or voting rights to th ose Direct Participants to whose accoun ts the 2021 Bonds ar e credited on the 
record date (identified in a listing attached to the Omnibus Proxy). 
Principal, premium, if any, and interest payments on the 2021 Bonds will be made to Cede & Co., or such other 
nominee as may be requested by an authorized representative of DTC.  DTC’s practice is to credit Direct Participants’ 
accounts, upon DTC’s receipt of funds and corresponding detailed information from the Commission or the Trustee, on 
the payment date in accordance with thei r respective holdings shown on DTC’s re cords.  Payments by Participants to 
Beneficial Owners will be governed by standing instructions and customary practices, as is the case with securities held 
for the accounts of customers in bearer form or registered  in “street name,” and will be the responsibility of such 
Participant and not of DTC, the Trustee, or the Commission, subject to any statutory or regulatory requirements as may 
be in effect from time to time.  Payment of principal, in terest and any other redemption payments to Cede & Co. (or 
such other nominee as may be requested by an authorized representative of DTC) is the responsibility of the Commission  
12 
or the Trustee, disbursement of such payments to Direct Participants will be the responsibility of DTC, and disbursement 
of such payments to the Beneficial Owners will be the responsibility of Direct and Indirect Participants. 
DTC may discontinue providing its services as securities depository with respect to the 2021 Bonds at any time 
by giving reasonable notice to the Commission or the Trustee.  Under such circumstances, in the event that a successor 
securities depository is not obtained, 2021 Bond certificates are required to be printed and delivered. 
The Commission may decide to discontinue use of the system of book entry only transfers through DTC (or a 
successor securities depository) with respect to the 2021  Bonds.  In that event, 2021 Bond certificates will be printed 
and delivered.  See “Certificated 2021 Bonds.” 
NEITHER THE COMMISSION NOR THE TRUSTEE HAS ANY RESPONSIBILITY OR OBLIGATION 
TO ANY PARTICIPANT OR THE PERSONS TO WHOM THEY ACT AS NOMINEES WITH RESPECT TO:  THE 
ACCURACY OF THE RECORDS MAINTAINED BY DTC, CEDE & CO. OR ANY PARTICIPANT; PAYMENTS 
TO, OR THE PROVIDING OF NOTICE FOR, ANY PARTICIPANT OR ANY INDIRECT PARTICIPANT OR 
BENEFICIAL OWNER; THE SELECTION BY DTC OR ANY PARTICIPANT OF ANY PERSON TO RECEIVE 
PAYMENT IN THE EVENT OF A PARTIAL REDEMPTION OF THE 2021 BONDS; OR ANY CONSENT GIVEN 
OR OTHER ACTION TAKEN BY DTC AS THE REGISTERED OWNER OF 2021 BONDS. 
The Commission and the Trustee have no role in the purchases, transfers or sales of book entry interests.  The 
rights of book entry interest owners to transfer or pledge their interests, and the manner of transferring or pledging those 
interests, may be subject to applicable state law.  Book entry interest owners may want to discuss with their legal advisers 
the manner of transferring or pledging their book entry interests. 
The Commission and Trustee have no responsibility or liability for any aspects of the records or notices relating 
to, or payments made on account of, book entry interest ownership, or for maintaining, supervising or reviewing any 
records relating to that ownership. 
For ease of reference in this and other discussions, reference to “DTC” includes when applicable any successor 
securities depository and the nominee of the depository. 
For all purposes under the Resolution, DTC will be and will be, considered by the Commission and the Trustee 
to be, the owner or holder of the 2021 Bonds. 
Owners of book entry interests in th e 2021 Bonds (book entry interest owners) will not receive or have the 
right under the Resolution to receive physical delivery of the 2021 Bonds. 
Certificated 2021 Bonds. The Commission may decide to discontinue use of the system of book entry transfers 
through DTC (or a successor s ecurities depository) with respect to the 20 21 Bonds.  If for any reason the book entry 
only system is discontinued, the 2021 Bond certificates will be delivered as described in the Resolution and the 
Beneficial Owner, upon registration of certificates held in  the Beneficial Owner’s name, will become the Bondholder.  
Thereafter, 2021 Bonds may be exchanged for an equal aggregate principal amount of 2021 Bonds in other authorized 
denominations, upon surrender thereof at the principal corporate trust office of the Trustee.  The transfer of any 2021 
Bond may be registered on the books maintained by the Trustee for such purpose only upon the surrender thereof to the 
Trustee with a duly executed assignment in form satisfactory to the Trustee.  For every exchange or registration of 
transfer of 2021 Bonds, the Commission and the Trustee may make a charge sufficient to reimburse them for any tax or 
other governmental charge required to be paid with respect to such exchange or registration of transfer, but no other 
charge may be made to the owner for any exchange or registration of transfer of the 2021 Bonds.

SECURITY FOR THE BONDS 
General 
The Bonds, including the 2021 Bonds, are general obligations of the Commission and the full faith and credit 
of the Commission are pledged to the payment of the principal and redemption price thereof and interest thereon, upon 
the terms provided in the Resolution.  Pursuant to the Act and the Resolution, the Commission has pledged and granted 
a security interest for the security and payment of the Bonds  in all Revenues (defined generally to include all income, 
revenues, receipts and other moneys derived by the Commi ssion from its ownership an d operation of the Systems, 
together with any existing or future rights of the Commission to receive the same, other than certain grant receipts and 
other moneys), subject only to the application of such Revenues for the purposes set forth in the Resolution, including 
without limitation the expenses of admini stration, operation and maintenance of the Systems in accordance with the 
terms and conditions of the Resolution.  See APPENDIX E and APPENDIX F.  The pledge and security interest for 
the security and payment of the Subordinated Bonds, if any, under the Resolution are subject to the pledge and security 
interest for Senior Bonds.  In addition, all other moneys and securities on deposit from time to time in all funds and 
accounts established by the Resolution, other than (i) the Subordinated Debt Service Reserve Fund with respect to Senior 
Bonds, (ii) the Senior Redemption Account, the Senior Debt Service Fund and the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund 
with respect to Subordinated Bonds, and (iii) the General Fund and the Rebate Fund with respect to all Bonds, are 
pledged and subject to a security interest for the benefit of the owners of Bonds until such moneys are properly disbursed.  
Such funds and accounts include the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund, Operating Reserve Fund, Renewal and 
Replacement Reserve Fund, Insurance Reserve Fund, Stabilization Fund and other funds discussed below. 
Debt service on and the redemption price of Senior Bonds are payable from the Senior Debt Service Fund and 
the Senior Redemption Account of the Redemption Fund.  Debt service on and the redemption price of Subordinated 
Bonds are payable from the Subordinat ed Debt Service Fund and the Subordinated Redemption Account of the 
Redemption Fund.  Th e various funds and accounts esta blished under the Resolution, th e flow of Revenues through 
such funds and accounts, the rights and remedies of Bond holders under the Resolution and other related matters are 
summarized in APPENDIX F and under “Flow of Funds” herein. 
The Resolution permits the issuance of bond anticipation notes (“Bond Anticipation Notes”) whenever a Series 
of Bonds is authorized and allows proceeds of the Series of Bonds in anticipation of which Bond Anticipation Notes are 
issued to be pledged for such purpose.  In addition, interest to come due on such Bond Anticipation Notes may be 
secured by a subordinate lien on Revenues.  On November 15, 2006, the Commission authorized up to $125 million of 
such Bond Anticipation Notes to be  outstanding at any one time until D ecember 12, 2037 designated as the 
Commission’s Tax Exempt Commercial Paper Bond Anticipation Notes, Series A.  
The 2021 Bonds will constitute Senior Bonds under the Resolution and, notwithstanding their date or dates of 
issuance or maturity, all Senior Bonds will be secured, equally and ratably without preference of any such Senior Bond 
over any other such Senior Bond by the pledges created by and covenants of the Commission made in the Resolution.  
The Commission expects to issue Additional Bonds under the Resolution on parity with the 2021 Bonds and other 
Outstanding Senior Bonds.  For a description of the Commission’s currently Outstanding Bonds, see FINANCIAL 
OPERATIONS “-Outstanding Indebtedness” herein. 
The Act provides that the Commission is subject to suit, but that the property of the Commission, other than 
Revenues pledged to the payment of the Bonds, is not subject to attachment or levy by execution to satisfy a judgment 
(including any judgment for the benefit of the 2021 Bonds).  The Commission has no taxing power.  Neither the City of 
Boston nor the Commonwealth nor any other political subdivis ion thereof other than the Commission is obligated to 
pay the principal of and interest and premium, if any, on the Bonds, and neither the faith and credit nor the taxing power 
of the City or the Commonwealth or any other such political subdivision thereof, is pledged to such payment. 
The enforceability of the Bonds and the Resolution may be limited by the exercise of judicial discretion in 
accordance with general equitable principles and by bankruptcy, reorganization, insolvency, moratorium and other laws 
affecting creditors’ rights generally heretofore or hereafter enacted to the extent constitutionally enforceable.  
14 
Rate Covenants 
The Act provides that fees, rates, rents, bettermen ts, assessments and other charges established by the 
Commission for water, sewer and other services, facilities and commodities furnis hed or supplied by it, shall not be 
subject to supervision or regulation by any department, division, commission, board, bureau or agency of the 
Commonwealth or of the City or any of their respective political subdivisions.  Under the MWRA’s enabling act, the 
Commission is required, however, to give written notice to  the MWRA of proposed rules and regulations, including 
rates, relating to its water and sewer se rvices prior to their adoption.  The Commission is required under the Act, and 
has covenanted in the Resolution, to maintain rates and char ges adequate at all times, with other available funds, to 
provide Revenues and other moneys at least sufficient, with such margin of safety as the Commission deems necessary, 
to pay or provide for all Operating Expenses and MWRA assessments, all payments of principal, premium and interest 
on all Outstanding Bonds, including the 2021 Bonds, Subordinated Bonds and any other indebtedness of or assumed by 
the Commission, including any Bond Anticipation Notes, all amounts payable to the reserve funds maintained under the 
Resolution, all repairs, replacements and renewals of the Systems deemed necessary by the Commission, and all other 
amounts which the Commission may by law or contract be obligated to pay.  The Act further requires the Commission 
to maintain its books and records in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles and that an annual audit 
be performed by an independent certified public accounting firm. 
Without limiting the generality of the foregoing covenant, so long as any Bonds are Outstanding, the 
Commission has also covenanted in the Resolution to maintain rates and charges at levels so that total Net Revenues in 
each Fiscal Year will equal at least 125% of the principal,  sinking fund payments, and interest due on all Outstanding 
Bonds (the “Bond Debt Service Requirement”) during such Fiscal Year calculated as of the first day of such Fiscal Year 
less the amount, if any, of Bond proceeds av ailable as of the first day of the Fis cal Year to pay interest becoming due 
on Bonds Outstanding as of the first day of such Fiscal Year.  See APPENDIX F - Summary of Certain Provisions 
of the Resolution - “Covenant as to Rates and Charges” for a more detailed description of the foregoing covenant.  
For purposes of this covenant, Net Revenues are defined by the Resolution to mean all Revenues (excluding proceeds 
of insurance, condemnation or the sale or other disposition of any part of the Systems) received in a Fiscal Year and 
deposited in the Revenue Fund, including any amounts on de posit in the Stabilization Fund (“Reserved Revenues”) at 
the beginning of such Fiscal Year which the Commission has directed to be deposited in the Revenue Fund during such 
year, less all amounts withdrawn from the Revenue Fund during the Fiscal Year and deposited in any fund and account 
under the Resolution other than the Senior Debt Service Fund, Subordinated Debt Service Fund, Renewal and 
Replacement Account, Renewal and Replacement Reserve Fund , the Stabilization Fund (le ss withdrawals from such 
Fund during such Fiscal Yea r), any Temporary Project Accoun t and the General Fund.  See APPENDIX E  and 
APPENDIX F. 
Failure by the Commission to comply with the foregoing rate covenant in any Fiscal Year will not constitute 
an Event of Default under the Resolution, so long as the Commission promptly and diligently takes such steps as are 
permitted by law and as are necessary to  cure or avoid the deficiency in the next succeeding Fiscal Year.  The 
Commission is required to furnish the Trustee annually wi th a certificate stating that the Commission satisfied the 
foregoing rate covenant in the preceding Fiscal Year or, if such was not the cas e, stating the corrective steps taken by 
the Commission.  The Commission’s certificate must be accompanied by a certificate of an independent public 
accountant setting forth the Net Revenues for the prior Fiscal Year. 
If at the end of any Fiscal Year th e Commission has realized a surplus fro m operations for such Fiscal Year, 
after payment or provision for all current operating expenses, current debt service, all reserves for debt service, repairs 
and replacements or other capital or current expenses of the Systems and any other amounts which the Commission may 
be obligated to pay or provide for by law or contract (including the Resolution), the Commission is required under the 
Act either to apply such surplus to a reduction in its rates an d charges in the next Fiscal Y ear or to pay the amount of 
such surplus to the City for application to such purposes as the City may deem appropriate.  If at the end of any Fiscal 
Year the Commission has realized a deficit from operations for such Fiscal Year, the Commission is required under the 
Act to recover such deficit by increasing its rate s and charges in the follo wing Fiscal Year.  See FINANCIAL 
OPERATIONS
 for a discussion of the Commission’s historical, current and projected rates, revenues and expenses and 
rate-setting procedures.  
15 
Flow of Funds 
Under the Resolution, all Revenues (except certain sa le, insurance and condemnation proceeds and certain 
investment earnings) are deposited in the Revenue Fund held by the Trustee.  The Resolution provides that the Trustee 
make monthly transfers as required from the Revenue Fund to the other funds and accounts and in the order as shown 
in the chart that follows.  Each fund and account must be funded from Revenues to the amount required under the 
Resolution before Revenues are transferred to funds and accounts lower in the flow of funds.  The following chart should 
be read in conjunction with APPENDIX E and APPENDIX F. 
Revenue Fund -- Receives Revenues and additional moneys deposited therein by Commission at its 
discretion. 
 
Operating Account -- Monthly deposit in amount provided in Commission’s Annual Budget. 
 
Renewal and Replacement Account -- Monthly deposit in amount provided in Commission’s Capital 
Improvement Budget. 
 
Senior Debt Service Fund -- Monthly deposit in amount equal, together with other funds on deposit, to 
accrued but unpaid debt service on Senior Bonds. 
 
Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund -- Deposit as needed to equal Senior Funded Debt Service Reserve 
Fund Requirement. 
 
Subordinated Debt Service Fund -- Monthly deposit in amount equal, together with other funds on 
deposit, to accrued but unpaid debt service on Subordinated Bonds. 
 
Subordinated Debt Service Reserve Fund -- Deposit as needed to equal Subordinated Funded Debt 
Service Reserve Fund Requirement. 
 
Stabilization Fund -- Deposits as needed to equal Stabilization Fund Requirement plus additional 
deposits as determined by Commission, provided other funds and accounts are funded at required levels. 
 
Operating Reserve Fund -- Deposits as needed to equal Operating Reserve Fund Requirement. 
 
Insurance Reserve Fund -- Deposits as determined by Commission to be necessary on the basis of an 
audit of outstanding claims. 
 
MDC (MWRA) Assessment Fund -- Monthly deposit of 1/12 of MWRA Assessments payable in 
Fiscal Year (or, during last two months, 1/12 due next Fiscal Year). 
 
Renewal and Replacement Reserve Fund -- Deposits as needed to equal Renewal and Replacement 
Reserve Fund Requirement. 
 
Temporary Project Accounts -- Deposit as requested by Commission for Capital Improvements. 
Balances remaining in the Revenue Fund after the a bove-described transfers may in the discretion of the 
Commission be applied to pay interest due on Bond Anticipation Notes.  Balances remaining in the Revenue Fund at 
the end of a Fiscal Year may be transferred to the General Fund held by the Commission.  The Commission has 
covenanted in its loan agreements with the MCWT, to set its rates and charges in each year so that there will be sufficient 
amounts in the Revenue Fund available to be transferred at the end of each Fiscal Year to the General Fund to pay the 
net debt service due on the Commission’s loans fr om MCWT in the succeeding Fiscal Year.  See FINANCIAL 
OPERATIONS - “Outstanding Indebtedness.” Amounts are transferred to the Re demption Fund when required for 
the redemption of the Bonds.  Amounts on deposit in the various funds and accounts described above must be transferred 
to either the Senior Debt Service Fund or Subordinated De bt Service Fund to the extent that the amounts on deposit 
therein and various other funds such as the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund or Subordinated Debt Service Reserve 
Fund are insufficient to pay debt service on Senior Bonds or Subordinated Bonds when due; provided, however, that no  
16 
such transfers may be made from the Operating Account, from the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund for the benefit of 
Subordinated Bonds or from the Subordinated Debt Service Reserve Fund for the benefit of Senior Bonds. 
Reserve Funds and Stabilization Fund 
As additional security for the 2021 Bonds and all other Outstanding Senior Bonds, the Resolution establishes 
a Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund to be maintained in an amount at least equal to the sum, as of any computation date, 
of (i) the maximum amount of principal or sinking fund payments and interest to become due in the current or any 
succeeding Fiscal Year on the Outstanding Senior Bonds issued as “Fixed Rate Bonds,” net of any accrued interest from 
the sale of any such Bonds, and (ii) with respect to Ou tstanding Senior Bonds issued as  “Variable Rate Bonds,” the 
maximum amount of principal and interest projected to be come due in the current or any succeeding Fiscal Year on a 
hypothetical, Pro Forma Fixed Rate Bond  Issue reasonably determined by the Commission at the time of issuance of 
such Bonds to be the equivalent of the Variable Rate Bonds if such Variable Rate Bonds had been issued as Fixed Rate 
Bonds (such sum being the “Senior Debt Service Reserve F und Requirement”).  In lieu of cash or securities, the 
Resolution permits the Commission to satisfy the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund Requirement in part or in whole 
by maintaining (i) irrevocable and unconditional policies of insurance from municipal bond insurers (surety bonds) with 
a credit rating within the two highest rating categories availa ble generally to issuers of such insurance from Moody’s 
Investors Service, Inc. (“Moody’s”) and S&P, or (ii) irrevocable, unconditional and unexpired letters of credit from 
banking institutions having a credit rating within the two highest rating categories generally available to banking 
institutions from Moody’s and S&P, in each case making funds available to the Trustee for the same purpose and subject 
to the same conditions as such cash or securities would be available (such insurance and letters of credit being “Reserve 
Requirements”). 
If at any time the amounts on deposit in the Senior Debt Service Fund, the Senior Redemption Account of the 
Redemption Fund and the Stabilization Fund under the Resolu tion are insufficient to pay the principal or redemption 
price of and interest on the 2021 Bonds or any other Senior Bonds then due, first, moneys in the Senior Debt Service 
Reserve Fund will be applied to the deficiency by the Trustee and second, to the extent necessary, draws or claims will 
be made under any Reserve Requirements applicable to such Fund.  If moneys or any Reserve Requirement in the Senior 
Debt Service Reserve Fund are applied to the payment of debt service, the Resolution provides for the restoration of the 
Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund to an amount at least equal to the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund Requirement 
less the stated and unpaid amount of any Reserve Requir ement through monthly deposits from the Revenue Fund. 
Investments in the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund will be  valued at amortized cost unless and until the Trustee is 
required to withdraw moneys from such Fund, whereupon investments will be valued at the lesser of amortized cost or 
market value until the Fund balance again equals the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund Requirement.  Upon the issuance 
of the 2021 Bonds, the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund will be funded in the amount of the Senior Debt Service 
Reserve Fund Requirement. As of December 31, 2020, the unaudited balance in the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund 
was $45.5 million. 
The Stabilization Fund also is ple dged as security for all Bonds an d the Commission’s obligations.  The 
Resolution currently contains a Stabilization Fund Requirement of four percent (4%) of the aggregate principal amount 
of Variable Rate Bonds Outstanding, which requirement was approximately $0.4 million as of December 31, 2020.  
From time to time, the Commission may deposit additional moneys in the Stabilization Fund to mitigate rate increases 
in upcoming years and may withdraw mone ys from the Stabilization Fund for such  rate increase mitigation.  As of 
December 31, 2020, the unaudited balan ce in the Stabilization Fund was $42.6 million.  Follo wing projected deposits 
in Fiscal Years 2022 through 2025, the Commission’s financial forecast anticipates that the Stabilization Fund will have 
a balance of $60.7 million as of December 31, 2025.  See HISTORICAL REVENUES AND EXPENSES – 
“Projected Revenues and Expenses.” 
In addition to the Senior Debt Service Reserve Fund, the Resolution establishes as reserve funds an Operating 
Reserve Fund, a Renewal and Replacement Reserve Fund and an Insurance Reserve Fund.  Such funds are pledged as 
security for all Bonds, subject to the terms of the Resolutio n.  Each of these reserve funds will be fully funded in the 
amounts of their respective requirements on the date of delivery of the 2021 Bonds.  The Subordinated Debt Service 
Reserve Fund established under the Resolution is not pledged as security for the 2021 Bonds or any other Senior Bonds.  
In accordance with the provisions of the Resolution, moneys deposited in the Operating Reserve Fund, which 
is required to be maintained in an amount at least equal to the Operating Reserve Fund Requirement, will be drawn in 
the event of unexpected and unbudgeted Operating Expenses and MWRA assessments or a shortfall in Revenues. As of 
December 31, 2020, the unaudited balance in the Operating Reserv e fund was $54.3 million. The Renewal and 
Replacement Reserve Fund may be used to pay the costs of emergency or otherwise unexpected Capital Improvements  
17 
and will be maintained in an amount approximately equal to 25% of the then current Fiscal Year’s renewal and 
replacement expenditures. As of December 31, 2020, the unaudited balance in the Renewal and Replacement Reserve 
Fund was $4.3 million.  
The Insurance Reserve Fund is required to be maintained in an amount determined by the Commission, with 
the advice of its insurance consultant, to be sufficient to reserve against property and personal injury risks for which the 
Commission is self-insured. As of December 31, 2020, the unaudited balance of the Insu rance Reserve Fund totaled 
$1.7 million.  In May 2021, the Commission’s risk management consultant completed a review of all of the outstanding 
property damage and personal injury cl aims on file at the Commission as of  December 31, 2020, and based on such 
review, recommended that the Insurance Reserve Fund be maintained at approximately $2.0 million. The Commission 
will make a deposit to the Insurance Reserve Fund, in the amount of approximately $0.3 million, by the end of 2021 to 
satisfy the reserve requirement.  
Additional Bonds and Refunding Bonds 
The Resolution permits the issuance of one or more Series of Additional Bonds (“Additional Bonds”) on a 
parity with or subordinate to the 2021 Bonds for the purpose of paying the Cost of any Project, making deposits in 
various funds established under the Resolution, paying Costs of Issuance, paying the principal of and premium and 
interest on any notes issued in anticipation of such Additional Bonds or any combination of the foregoing.  Bonds may 
be issued as Subordinated Bonds or as Senior Bonds as to security and, without limitation, as Variable Rate Bonds (as 
defined in the Resolution), Fixed Rate Bonds (as defined in the Resolution), Bonds providing for the right of the owner 
thereof to present the Bond for redemption or purchase prior to maturity, zero interest rate or deep discount Bonds, 
Bonds providing for the compounding of interest, or any combination thereof.  Bonds may be issued or outstanding 
from time to time with or without credit enhancement provisions. 
Additional Bonds may be issued by the Commission only upon receipt by the Trustee of, among other things, 
the following: 
(1) a certificate of the Commission (a) setting forth th e amount of Net Revenues for the last full Fiscal 
Year prior to the Fiscal Year in which such Additional Bonds are issued and (b) showing that the Net 
Revenues in such Fiscal Year were equal to at least 125% of (i) the Bond Debt Service Requirement 
during such Fiscal Year less (ii) the amount, if any, of Bond proceeds available to pay principal and 
interest coming due in such Fiscal Year on Bonds Outstanding as of the first day of such Fiscal Year; 
and  
(2) a certificate of a consulting engineer (a) setting fo rth the estimated annual Net Revenues for each of 
the five full Fiscal Years following the issuance of such Additional Bonds, and showing for each of 
such Fiscal Years that the estimated annual Net Revenues for such Fiscal Year together with the 
amounts of Reserved Revenues, calculated by the Commission, will be at least equal to 125% of (i) 
the aggregate of the Senior Debt Service Reserv e Fund Requirement and the Subordinated Debt 
Service Reserve Fund Requirement calculated as of the first day of such Fiscal Year less (ii) the 
amount, if any, of Bond proceeds available or projected to be available to pay principal and interest 
coming due in such Fiscal Year on Bonds Outstanding or projected to be Outstanding as of the first 
day of such Fiscal Year. 
The Commission may issue Refunding Bonds only upon certifying that the aggregate debt service in each 
Fiscal Year in which the Refunding Bo nds are Outstanding will not be increase d as a result of the issuance of the 
Refunding Bonds; provided that, in lieu of such certifica tion, the Commission may deliver to the Trustee certificates 
satisfying the conditions described above for the issuance of Additional Bonds.   
A more detailed description of the requirements relating to the issuance of Additional Bonds is set forth in 
APPENDIX F - Summary of Certain Provisions of the Resolution - “Additional Bonds and Refunding Bonds.”
